# Context Switch Response 23 :

**Switch Prompt - Decision Companion Project Handoff**

**ЁЯОп Project Summary**

**Project Name:** Decision Companion System **Purpose:** Multi-criteria decision support tool for Vonue take-home assignment **Deadline:** March 2, 2026 **Current Status:** Phase 1 complete and tested, ready for documentation

**тЬЕ What\'s Been Built (Phase 1 Complete)**

**Core Algorithm (100% Our Logic, No AI)**

-   **File:** backend/decisionLogic.js

-   **Method:** Weighted penalty scoring with distance-from-ideal-point

-   **Features Implemented:**

    -   Normalization (all values тЖТ 0-100 scale for fair comparison)

    -   Direction-aware penalties (higher-is-better vs lower-is-better)

    -   Weighted aggregation (user importance ratings тЖТ normalized weights)

    -   Tie detection with float tolerance (╬╡ \< 0.001)

    -   Ranking output (sorted by total penalty score)

**Web Interface**

-   **Stack:** Node.js + Express backend, vanilla HTML/CSS/JS frontend

-   **Port:** localhost:3000

-   **Flow:** 5-step wizard

    1.  Setup (number of products/features)

    2.  Define criteria (name, importance 1-5, direction)

    3.  Enter product values

    4.  Enter ideal values

    5.  View results with ranking + explanations

**Explanation System (Multi-Source with Fallback Chain)**

-   **Primary:** Groq API (Llama 3.3-70B) - Fast, free tier

-   **Backup:** Gemini API (gemini-2.5-flash) - If Groq fails

-   **Final Fallback:** Template-based (offline, always works)

-   **Feature:** 4 explanation styles (Data-Driven, Storytelling, Comparative, Actionable) with refresh button to cycle through

-   **Quality Gate:** Rejects short AI responses (\<50 words), falls back to detailed template

**Testing Results**

-   **10 Manual Test Cases:** All passed тЬЕ

    -   Basic scenarios (laptops, jobs, travel)

    -   Edge cases (ties, extreme weights, unreachable ideals)

    -   Test Case 9 initially appeared to fail but manual verification proved system correct

**ЁЯРЫ Critical Bugs Fixed During Development**

**Bug 1: Normalization Scale Mismatch (Feb 16, Morning)**

-   **Issue:** Comparing normalized product values (0-100) to raw ideal values

-   **Impact:** Completely wrong results

-   **Fix:** Normalize ideal values using same min/max formula

-   **Location:** decisionLogic.js lines 37-45

**Bug 2: Double Penalty Calculation (Feb 16, Afternoon)**

-   **Issue:** d\[i\]\[y\] = abs(actual - ideal) + penalty тЖТ counted penalty twice

-   **Impact:** All scores 2x too high

-   **Fix:** Changed to d\[i\]\[y\] = penalty only

-   **Location:** decisionLogic.js lines 58-67

**Bug 3: API Confusion - Grok vs Groq (Feb 17)**

-   **Issue:** Calling api.x.ai (xAI\'s Grok) instead of api.groq.com (Groq/Llama)

-   **Impact:** 400/403 errors on all API calls

-   **Fix:** Learned correct patterns from Antigravity project server.js

    -   Groq: api.groq.com, model llama-3.3-70b-versatile

    -   Gemini: Key in URL (?key=), model gemini-2.5-flash

**Bug 4: One-Line Explanation Collapse (Feb 18)**

-   **Issue:** Multi-line explanations rendering as single compressed line

-   **Impact:** Comparative/Action styles unreadable

-   **Fix:** Added white-space: pre-line; to .explanation-card p in CSS

-   **Additional Fix:** Quality gate to reject short AI responses

\## ЁЯзо Algorithm Details (For Documentation)

\### Input

\- \`n\` products (n тЙе 2 recommended)

\- \`f\` features (f тЙе 1)

\- Importance ratings per feature (1-5 scale, auto-normalized to sum = 1.0)

\- Direction per feature (True = higher better, False = lower better)

\- Ideal values per feature

\### Process

\`\`\`

1\. Compute min/max per feature across all products

2\. Normalize all product values: (value - min)/(max - min) ├Ч 100

3\. Normalize ideal values using same min/max

4\. Calculate penalties:

\- If higher-is-better: penalty = max(0, ideal - actual)

\- If lower-is-better: penalty = max(0, actual - ideal)

5\. Aggregate: total_penalty = ╬г(penalty\[i\] ├Ч weight\[i\])

6\. Rank by total penalty (ascending)

7\. Detect ties with ╬╡-tolerance (\|score1 - score2\| \< 0.001)

**Output**

-   Winner (or list of tied products)

-   Complete ranking with scores

-   Per-product, per-feature penalty breakdown

-   AI-generated explanation (or template fallback)

-   4 alternative explanation styles

**ЁЯОУ Design Decisions & Rationale (For README)**

  ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **Decision**        **Alternatives Considered**   **Chosen**                     **Reason**
  ------------------- ----------------------------- ------------------------------ -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **Backend**         Python Flask                  Node.js + Express              Prepares for Phase 2 web scraping, single-language stack

  **Frontend**        React, Vue                    Vanilla HTML/CSS/JS            No learning curve, sufficient for requirements, evaluators care about logic not framework

  **Algorithm**       TOPSIS, AHP, complex MCDM     Weighted penalty scoring       Explainable, transparent, sufficient for use case

  **Normalization**   Skip it, use raw values       Min-max to 0-100               Fair comparison across different scales (price in thousands, RAM in single digits)

  **AI Usage**        AI makes decision             AI only for explanation text   Meets \"not AI dependent\" requirement, core logic is ours

  **Explanation**     Template only                 Groq тЖТ Gemini тЖТ Template       Best of both: natural language when available, always works offline
  ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

\## тЪая╕П Known Limitations (To Document)

\### Current Limitations

1\. \*\*Requires numeric values\*\* - No support for qualitative criteria (e.g., \"good\", \"average\", \"poor\")

2\. \*\*Linear penalty model\*\* - No diminishing returns (gap from 0тЖТ10 same as 90тЖТ100)

3\. \*\*Singular ideal values\*\* - No range-based criteria support

4\. \*\*No data persistence\*\* - Session-based only, no database

5\. \*\*String comparison\*\* - \"True\"/\"False\" direction is case-sensitive in backend (handled by dropdown in UI)

\### Edge Cases Handled

\- Division by zero when all products identical on a feature тЖТ Set normalized value to 50.0

\- Ideal value outside product range тЖТ Normalization handles gracefully

\- Float comparison for ties тЖТ Epsilon tolerance (\< 0.001)

\- Weights sum validation тЖТ Auto-normalize if don\'t sum to 1.0

\-\--

\## ЁЯТм Questions That Might Come Up

\*\*Q: Why not use established MCDM methods like TOPSIS or AHP?\*\*

A: Explainability. Weighted penalty scoring is intuitive for users and transparent in showing how decisions are made. Complex methods would be black boxes.

\*\*Q: Why allow AI in explanation generation if assignment says \"not AI dependent\"?\*\*

A: Core decision logic (normalization, penalties, ranking) is 100% deterministic code. AI only converts our calculated numbers into natural language. Assignment allows AI if role is clearly justified.

\*\*Q: What if APIs are down during evaluation?\*\*

A: System has triple fallback (Groq тЖТ Gemini тЖТ Template). Template fallback works offline with zero dependencies. Evaluators will always get results.

\*\*Q: How do you handle subjective criteria?\*\*

A: Current version requires numeric values. User must convert subjective judgments to numbers (e.g., \"cultural fit\" тЖТ rate 1-10). Future enhancement could add categorical support.

\*\*Q: Why Node.js if you already wrote the algorithm in Python?\*\*

A: Prepares for Phase 2 (web scraping has better libraries in Node.js). Also demonstrates ability to convert logic across languages while maintaining correctness.

\-\--

# Response 25 : Phase 1.5

You\'ve touched on the \"Core Ambiguity\" of system design. To answer your question:┬а**Phase 1 is mathematically complete, but semantically limited.**

Currently, your system is a \"Logic Engine\" that needs a \"Translation Layer\" to handle the real world. Here are some natural language hints (Phase 1.5 concepts) on how we could bridge that gap without changing the core penalty-scoring logic:

**1. The \"Scale Mapping\" Strategy (The Low-Code Bridge)**

Instead of a free-text input, we could provide a┬а**Likert Scale**┬аin the UI.

-   *User sees:*┬а\"Communication: \[Excellent, Good, Average, Poor\]\"

-   *System processes:*┬а{Excellent: 10, Good: 7, Average: 5, Poor: 2}

-   **Why this works:**┬аIt converts subjective judgment into an objective number┬а*before*┬аthe math engine even sees it. It satisfies the \"Numerical Input\" requirement of Phase 1 while feeling subjective to the user.

**2. The \"Categorical Distance\" Strategy (The \"Weather\" Example)**

For things like \"Sunny\" vs \"Windy\", we can\'t use 0-100 logic easily.

-   **Hint:**┬аWe treat the values as a set. If the Ideal is \"Sunny\", and the product is \"Sunny\", penalty = 0. If it is \"Partly Cloudy\", penalty = 20. If it is \"Windy\", penalty = 50.

-   This requires a \"Distance Matrix\" where we define how far apart different qualitative categories are.

**3. The \"AI Sentiment Pre-Processor\" (The Phase 3 Preview)**

This is where the AI truly justifies its role.

-   **Concept:**┬аThe user inputs a review paragraph:┬а*\"The communication was okay but they lacked technical depth.\"*

-   **AI\'s Role:**┬аIt \"reads\" the text and outputs a JSON object:┬а

{Technical: 4, Communication: 6}

.

-   The AI acts as a┬а**feature extractor**┬аthat feeds your deterministic penalty engine. This ensures the┬а*decision*┬аis still based on your 100% logic, but the┬а*data entry*┬аis human-friendly.

**Is Phase 1 Complete?**

For the purpose of your assignment\'s Phase 1, yes---the engine works. But for a \"Decision Companion\" to be truly useful, it needs one of these bridges.

**Does one of these approaches (Mapping, Distance Sets, or AI Pre-processing) resonate with you for Phase 1.5/Phase 2?**┬аI\'ve updated the implementation plan to include a research task for this.

# Response 26 : Subjective Feedback Handling

Based on┬а**Vonnue\'s Prompt No. 1**┬аconditions and your Phase 1 logic, here is the breakdown of how to balance manual implementation vs. AI for Phase 1.5.

Vonnue\'s critical rule is:┬а**\"The system should not be a static hard-coded comparison\... but your logic should be explainable (not a black box).\"**

**My Recommendation (The \"Hints\")**

To wow the evaluators, don\'t let the AI \"decide\" the score. Use the AI to┬а**extract**┬аthe score from human language, while you handle the┬а**logic**.

1.  **The Manual \"Skeleton\" (Recommended for you to build):**┬аImplement a┬а

SubjectiveConverter

┬аfunction. This function checks if an input is in your manual┬а

EnumMapping

. If it is (e.g., the user selected \"Good\" from a dropdown), it uses your hard-coded value. This makes your system┬а**work offline**┬а(no AI needed).

2.  **The AI \"Translator\" (Justified Role):**┬аIf the user types a free-form review like┬а*\"The weather was a bit chilly but mostly clear,\"*┬аyour┬а

SubjectiveConverter

┬аwon\'t find that in its table.┬а**This is where you call the AI.**

-   **Prompt Hint:**┬а\"Given the travel goal is \'Tropical Paradise\', score the sentiment of this review from 1-10 regarding \'Weather\'.\"

-   **Justification:**┬а\"AI is used strictly as a Natural Language Interpreter to convert qualitative human feedback into numerical data for our deterministic scoring engine.\"

**Why this follows Vonnue\'s conditions:**

-   **Transparent:**┬аYou can show exactly how \"Good\" becomes 7.

-   **Not AI-Dependent:**┬аThe system still functions perfectly if the API is down (using the manual Enums/Dropdowns).

-   **Explainable:**┬аThe final ranking isn\'t a \"Because ChatGPT said so\" result; it\'s \"Because the input was interpreted as 7, which created a penalty of 3 based on our weighted logic.\"

**Verdict:**┬аFor Phase 1.5,┬а**Manually implement the Enum and Categorical Mapping.**┬аUse AI only as a \"fail-safe\" or \"interpreter\" for free-text inputs that don\'t match your manual categories.

**Next Step Hint:**┬аLook into how you would structure a┬а

mapping.js

┬аfile that your┬а

decisionLogic.js┬аcan call before starting the normalization. Do you want to see a conceptual structure of that mapping logic? (No code, just the structure).

# Antigravity Prompt 27 : Distance Matrix Concept

Categorical Proximity 100% Manual. You build a \"Distance Matrix.\" If Ideal: Sunny and Actual: Windy, distance = 8. 0%. This is a structured lookup table. High. Shows \"Design Maturity.\" elaborate on this how do you manually implement this.. CRTICAL DONT GIVE ME EXACT CODE RATHER TEACH ME

# Response 27 : New Concept Explained

To manually implement┬а**Categorical Proximity**, you are essentially building a┬а**\"Mathematical Map of Similarity.\"**

In your Phase 1 code,┬а

Penalty = \|Ideal - Actual\|

. With categories like \"Sunny\" vs \"Windy\", the computer doesn\'t know the \"distance\" between words. You have to define that distance manually.

Here is the conceptual breakdown of how to build this \"Logic Bridge\" without using AI:

**1. The \"Distance Matrix\" Concept**

Imagine a spreadsheet where every possible category is both a Row and a Column. The value in each cell represents the \"Penalty\" for that specific combination.

-   **Logic:**┬аIf the user wants \"Sunny\" (Ideal) and the destination is \"Rainy\" (Actual), your code looks up the intersection and finds an┬а**8 penalty**.

-   **Design Maturity:**┬аThis proves you've thought about the┬а*relationship*┬аbetween choices (e.g., \"Cloudy\" is closer to \"Sunny\" than \"Rainy\" is).

**2. The Implementation Logic (The \"How-To\")**

Instead of a simple subtraction, your┬а

decisionLogic.js┬аwould follow these steps:

1.  **Storage:**┬аStore these tables as nested \"Objects\" (Key-Value pairs). One object per feature (e.g.,┬а

weatherDistances

,┬а

colorDistances

).

2.  **The Fetcher:**┬аCreate a function that takes┬а

(FeatureName, ValueA, ValueB).

3.  **The Step-Down:**

    -   If┬а

ValueA == ValueB

, distance is┬а**0**.

-   Look into your┬а

DistanceMatrix

┬аfor┬а

ValueA

.

-   Inside that, look for┬а

ValueB

.

-   If found, that is your┬а**Penalty**.

-   If NOT found (user typed something weird), assign a┬а**Default Max Penalty**┬а(e.g., 10).

**3. The \"Ideal\" Problem**

In Phase 1, you allow users to type raw numbers for Ideals. For Categorical Proximity, you must limit the Ideal to a┬а**Dropdown Choice**.

-   If the feature type is \"Categorical,\" the UI should force the user to pick from your pre-defined map keys (Sunny, Cloudy, etc.).

**Why this is \"High Design Maturity\":**

When you explain this to Vonnue, you can say:

*\"I rejected the idea of letting the AI guess if \'Windy\' is better than \'Rainy\'. Instead, I built a deterministic Proximity Matrix. This ensures that the system\'s decision-making process is 100% transparent and consistent, while still allowing for qualitative criteria that simple math cannot handle.\"*

**The \"Pro Tip\" for your BUILD_PROCESS:**

Mention that you use┬а**Symmetry**. In a good distance matrix, the distance from┬а*Sunny to Rainy*┬аshould be the same as┬а*Rainy to Sunny*. If they aren\'t, it\'s an \"Asymmetric Matrix\"---which is even more advanced!

**Does this \"Lookup Table\" logic make sense for how you\'d replace the┬а**

Math.abs()

**┬аsubtraction for words?**

# Response 29 : Design Solutions to 6 Problems

Great questions --- all 6 are design decisions, not just coding questions. Let me walk through each one using your┬а**Juice example**┬аspecifically.

**Doubt 1: Must the Ideal Input Type Match the Feature Type?**

**Yes, ideally (pun intended).**┬аHere is why:

-   Feature:┬а**Price (Numeric)**┬атЖТ Ideal should also be a┬а**number**┬а(e.g.,┬а

тВ╣50

).

-   Feature:┬а**Quality (Scale)**┬атЖТ Ideal should be a┬а**Scale grade**┬а(e.g.,┬а

Excellent

).

-   Feature:┬а**Expert Opinion (Review)**┬атЖТ Ideal should be a┬а**short description**, NOT a review paragraph.

For \"Expert Opinion,\" the ideal could be a short target phrase that┬а*the user provides once*, like:

*\"I want a juice that is healthy and tasty.\"*

This is your┬а**reference point.**┬аEvery product\'s review is then scored against this one short ideal description. The user doesn\'t write 4 separate ideals --- just one target intention.

**Key Rule:**┬а

\"I hope its a price that doesn\'t sadden my heart\"

┬аis not a valid numeric ideal. The UI should enforce type-matching --- if the feature is Numeric, the ideal input box should be┬а

type=\"number\"

┬аonly.

**Doubt 2: When Does the AI Process the Reviews, and Can There Be a Loading Screen?**

**Yes, loading is necessary and there\'s a natural pause point.**

The timeline is:

User fills Step 3 (reviews for 4 products)

тЖУ

User fills Step 4 (ideal: \"Healthy, Tasty juice\")

тЖУ

User clicks \"Calculate Decision ЁЯЪА\"

тЖУ

Backend receives everything тЖТ NOW calls Gemini (This is the wait)

Loading UI: \"Optimizing to requirements\...\" тЖТ \"Calculating scores\...\" тЖТ \"Ranking results\...\"

тЖУ

Results appear.

The loading animation appears┬а**after**┬аthe user clicks Calculate and┬а**before**┬аresults are shown. This is already where your┬а

calculateResult()┬аdoes its┬а

fetch()

┬а--- you just add a loading overlay there.

**Doubt 3: What If Reviews Are Pure Trash (\"Taj Mahal is beautiful\")?**

This is a┬а**Garbage-in, Garbage-out**┬аproblem. Your options:

1.  **AI returns a low score automatically.**┬аIf Gemini reads \"Taj Mahal is beautiful\" against the ideal \"Healthy, Tasty juice,\" it cannot find any feature match тЖТ it should return \~1 or 2. This is actually correct behavior: an irrelevant review = nearly 0 quality signal.

2.  **Confidence flag.**┬аYou can instruct Gemini to return┬а

{\"score\": 2, \"confidence\": \"low\"}

┬аinstead of just┬а

2

. If confidence is┬а

\"low\"

, you surface a warning:┬а*\"тЪая╕П The AI found this review irrelevant to \'\${featureName}\'. Consider replacing it.\"*┬а--- but still proceed.

3.  (Optional)┬а**Pre-validation prompt.**┬аBefore scoring, ask Gemini: \"Is this text relevant to the feature \'\${featureName}\'? Reply YES or NO.\" If NO, ask the user to re-enter.

**Recommended for Phase 1.5:**┬аOption 2 (confidence flag). Simple, does not block the user, and shows transparency in your documentation.

**Doubt 4: Individual Score Per Review, or Comparative Feedback Across All 4?**

**Individual, without comparative context. Here\'s why with your example:**

Ideal: \"Healthy, Tasty juice\"

Review1: \"Very healthy but not tasty\" тЖТ Gemini scores: 6

Review2: \"Not healthy\" тЖТ Gemini scores: 2

Review3: \"Very tasty\" тЖТ Gemini scores: 6

Review4: \"Very Healthy\" тЖТ Gemini scores: 8

Gemini gets┬а**one call per product-feature pair.**┬аIt sees:

-   featureName

: \"Expert Opinion\"

-   idealDescription

: \"Healthy, Tasty juice\"

-   reviewText

: \"Very healthy but not tasty\"

-   Outputs:┬а

6

**It does NOT know about Review2, 3, or 4.**┬аWhy?

-   **Transparency:**┬аIf you send all 4 together and ask for ranks, the AI makes the decision --- which violates Vonnue\'s rule (\"not AI dependent\").

-   **Determinism:**┬аSending them one-by-one means each score is independent. Your penalty engine then does the comparing --- not the AI.

Think of the AI as a┬а**\"translator.\"**┬аIt converts┬а

\"Very healthy but not tasty\"

┬атЖТ┬а

6

. Your engine then calculates┬а

penalty = max(0, 10 - 6) = 4

. The┬а*comparison*┬аbetween 4 products is done by your math, not by Gemini.

**Doubt 5: Do You Need an Approval Stage Where the User Verifies AI Scores?**

**This is the most impactful design decision.**┬аYes, and here is how it works:

If the user clicks┬а**\"ЁЯФД Change\"**┬аon one row, that row turns into the Scale dropdown (Excellent тЖТ Poor). The user picks manually, and only that one score is replaced. Then they click \"Confirm & Calculate.\"

**Why this is gold for Vonnue:**

*\"The AI suggests scores, but the human always has final control. This ensures the system is AI-assisted, not AI-dependent.\"*

For 3 products ├Ч 3 reviewable features = 9 AI scores тЖТ 9 rows in the approval table.

**Doubt 6: Send Context Per Feature or Per All 12 Reviews?**

**Per Feature. Always.**┬аHere\'s the comparison:

**Option A --- All 12 reviews at once:**

-   You send 12 reviews + 3 ideals in one giant prompt.

-   Gemini must figure out which review belongs to which feature.

-   Errors in attribution are unpredictable and untraceable.

-   If one review fails the score, you can\'t retry just that one.

**Option B --- Per Feature (Recommended):**

-   For \"Expert Opinion\" тЖТ 1 API call per product (4 calls).

-   Each call has exactly:┬а

featureName

,┬а

idealDescription

,┬а

reviewText

.

-   Clean, atomic, and retryable.

-   Total for your 3-feature, 3-product example: 9 calls (only for \"review\" type features).

**The 9 calls happen in parallel**┬а(

Promise.all

) so the total wait time is the time of the┬а*slowest single call*, not 9├Ч the time.

Want me to update the implementation plan with these decisions baked in, especially the┬а**Approval Stage**┬а(Doubt 5), which is a significant new UI step?

# Antigravity Prompt 30 to Claude : Implement it

Summary Table: Design Decisions for Phase 1.5 Doubt Decision Ideal type matching тЬЕ Yes, UI enforces same type Loading screen тЬЕ Yes, between \"Calculate\" click and results Trash reviews тЪая╕П Confidence flag + user warning, but proceed Individual vs comparative тЬЕ Individual (per product-feature pair) Approval stage тЬЕ Yes, user can override before final calculation Context scope тЬЕ Per Feature, parallel API calls Want me to update the implementation plan with these decisions baked in, especially the Approval Stage (Doubt 5), which is a significant new UI step? #Vonnue\'s Mail Dear Candidate, Congratulations on being shortlisted from the programming test conducted at your college. As the next step in our evaluation process, we would like you to complete a take-home assignment. This round is intentionally different from a traditional coding test. You are allowed to use any resources - AI tools (ChatGPT, Copilot, etc.), Google, Stack Overflow, documentation, books, or any other reference material. We are not only evaluating the final solution. As our CEO puts it: "We want to see how you build." This assignment is designed to evaluate: 1. How clearly you document your thinking 2. How you approach ambiguous problems 3. Your system design and architectural decisions 4. How you leverage tools (including AI) 5. Your transparency in the build process Problem Statement: Design and build a "Decision Companion System" that helps a user make better decisions. The system should assist a user in evaluating options for a real-world decision of their choice. Your system must work without relying entirely on an AI model. If AI is used, clearly justify its role and limitations. Examples (you are NOT limited to these): \* Choosing a laptop under a budget \* Selecting the best candidate for a job role \* Deciding where to travel within constraints \* Picking an investment strategy \* Choosing a tech stack for a startup Core Expectations: Your system must: \* Accept multiple options \* Accept criteria (which may have different weights or importance) \* Process and evaluate options against criteria \* Provide a ranked recommendation \* Explain why a particular recommendation was made Beyond this, the design is up to you. You may choose: \* CLI / Web App / API / Desktop tool \* Any programming language \* Any framework \* Simple or advanced logic You define the depth. We are more interested in your thinking than feature count. Constraints \* The system should not be a static hard coded comparison. \* The user should be able to change inputs and get different outcomes. \* Your logic should be explainable (not a black box). Deliverables Please submit a Git repository containing: 1. Source Code \* Clean, readable, and structured \* Meaningful commit history 2. README.md Include: \* Your understanding of the problem \* Assumptions made \* Why you structured the solution the way you did \* Design decisions and trade-offs \* Edge cases considered \* How to run the project \* What you would improve with more time 3. Design Diagram Provide at least one: \* Architecture diagram \* Data flow diagram \* Component diagram \* Or decision logic diagram 4. BUILD_PROCESS.md Explain: \* How you started \* How your thinking evolved \* Alternative approaches considered \* Refactoring decisions \* Mistakes and corrections \* What changed during development and why 5. RESEARCH_LOG.md Include: \* All AI prompts used \* All search queries (including Google searches) \* References that influenced your approach \* What you accepted, rejected, or modified from AI outputs We are not judging you for using AI. We are evaluating how effectively and responsibly you use it. Evaluation Criteria You will be evaluated on: \* Clarity of thinking \* Problem structuring ability \* Quality of documentation \* Transparency in build process \* Design maturity \* Practical reasoning \* Code quality Timeline Submission deadline: On or before 02 March, 2026 We will be hosting a Google Meet on 21st February at 12:00 PM to address all your queries. Meanwhile if you have any other questions, please feel free to reach out to us via email. We are looking forward to seeing how you build.

PHASE A --- Penalty Ball Materializes:

a\. Show equation text above candidate in math zone:

Line1: \`\${feat}: \${raw} тЖТ norm: \${normed}\`

Line2: \`Penalty = max(0, \${normedIdeal} - \${normed}) = \${penalty}\`

b\. Compute ball brightness from penalty (0=transparent, 100=max glow)

c\. Materialize laser ball at BALL_ZONE_Y above CENTERS\[i\]

\- Size: fixed BASE_RADIUS (e.g. 28px) at this stage

\- Color: penalty=0 тЖТ transparent + colored border only

penalty\>0 тЖТ glowing, higher penalty = brighter/more saturated

\- Use PIXI.Graphics with Pixi filters (BlurFilter for glow effect)

\- Ball pulses gently (scale oscillation via ticker)

d\. await delay(1200)

4\. After all 3 balls materialized --- pause 800ms so user sees all 3

5\. For each candidate i (one at a time):

PHASE B --- Weight Applied, Ball Fires:

a\. Update equation text:

\`Weighted Penalty = \${penalty} ├Ч \${weight} = \${weightedPenalty}\`

b\. Ball grows from BASE_RADIUS to WEIGHTED_RADIUS

WEIGHTED_RADIUS = BASE_RADIUS + weight \* 60 (bigger = heavier weight)

Animate scale over 600ms

c\. weightedPenalty value text appears INSIDE the ball

d\. Ball fires DOWN toward character:

\- Animate y from BALL_ZONE_Y to character y over 800ms

\- Easing: accelerate (ease-in)

e\. On impact:

\- If penalty = 0: green tick тЬУ appears, no platform sink

\- If penalty \> 0: platform sinks, character shakes

\- Flash effect at impact point

f\. runPenalty\[i\] += weightedPenalty

g\. await updateEmos() (sequential, existing logic)

h\. await delay(400)

6\. Clear math zone text and balls

7\. Narrator reaction (existing logic)

**Laser Ball Visual Spec (Pixi Graphics)**

function makeLaserBall(penalty, maxPenalty) {

const t = Math.min(penalty / maxPenalty, 1); // 0 to 1

// Color: interpolate transparent тЖТ orange тЖТ red

// t=0: alpha=0, border only (0x4ade80 green border)

// t=0.5: 0xff9900 orange glow

// t=1: 0xff2200 red, intense

const ball = new PIXI.Graphics();

if (t \< 0.01) {

// Zero penalty --- transparent with green border

ball.lineStyle(2.5, 0x4ade80, 0.9);

ball.drawCircle(0, 0, BASE_RADIUS);

} else {

const r = Math.round(255);

const g = Math.round(150 \* (1 - t));

const color = (r \<\< 16) \| (g \<\< 8);

ball.beginFill(color, 0.15 + t \* 0.55);

ball.drawCircle(0, 0, BASE_RADIUS);

ball.endFill();

ball.lineStyle(2, color, 0.9);

ball.drawCircle(0, 0, BASE_RADIUS);

}

// Glow: use PIXI BlurFilter on a separate glow layer

// OR simulate with concentric circles at decreasing alpha

if (t \> 0.1) {

ball.beginFill(color, 0.06); ball.drawCircle(0,0, BASE_RADIUS\*1.6); ball.endFill();

ball.beginFill(color, 0.03); ball.drawCircle(0,0, BASE_RADIUS\*2.2); ball.endFill();

}

return ball;

}

**Pulse Animation (idle while waiting)**

function startPulse(ball) {

let t = 0;

const ticker = () =\> {

t += 0.04;

ball.scale.set(1 + Math.sin(t) \* 0.06);

};

app.ticker.add(ticker);

return ticker; // caller must remove when ball fires

}

**Fire Animation (ball drops to character)**

function fireBall(ball, pulseTicker, targetY) {

return new Promise(resolve =\> {

app.ticker.remove(pulseTicker);

ball.scale.set(1);

const startY = ball.y;

let t = 0;

const ticker = () =\> {

t += 0.018;

const ease = Math.pow(Math.min(t,1), 2); // ease-in (accelerate)

ball.y = startY + (targetY - startY) \* ease;

if (t \>= 1) {

app.ticker.remove(ticker);

fxL.removeChild(ball);

resolve();

}

};

app.ticker.add(ticker);

});

}

Whether you're working on a retro RPG, a roguelike, or a platformer, this fireball fits right in. Ideal For: Magic projectile attacks Enemy fireball shots Meteor rain effects Spellcasters and boss battles

# Codex Prompt 93 : CHANGES_fireball.md

**Fireball System --- Codex Implementation Spec**

**Asset Location**

frontend/sprites/fireballs/

fire_ball_side_small/imgs/ img_0.png ... img_29.png (30 frames)

fire_ball_side_medium/imgs/ img_0.png ... img_29.png (30 frames)

fireball_high_speed_side_small/imgs/ img_0.png ... img_39.png (40 frames)

meteor_side_medium/imgs/ img_0.png ... img_29.png (30 frames)

fire_ball_blue_side_small/imgs/ img_0.png ... img_34.png (35 frames)

All frames are 400x400px transparent PNG.

**Penalty тЖТ Fireball Type Mapping**

function getFireballType(penalty) {

if (penalty \< 0.01) return null; // zero тЖТ green ring only

if (penalty \<= 25) return \'fire_ball_side_small\';

if (penalty \<= 50) return \'fire_ball_side_medium\';

if (penalty \<= 75) return \'fireball_high_speed_side_small\';

return \'meteor_side_medium\';

}

function getFrameCount(type) {

if (type === \'fireball_high_speed_side_small\') return 40;

if (type === \'fire_ball_blue_side_small\') return 35;

return 30;

}

**Preload All Fireball Textures**

Add to loadTextures() --- load all frame arrays into:

const fireballTextures = {

fire_ball_side_small: \[\],

fire_ball_side_medium: \[\],

fireball_high_speed_side_small: \[\],

meteor_side_medium: \[\],

fire_ball_blue_side_small: \[\],

};

// In loadTextures(), for each type:

for (let f = 0; f \< frameCount; f++) {

const path = \`sprites/fireballs/\${type}/imgs/img\_\${f}.png\`;

fireballTextures\[type\].push(await PIXI.Assets.load(path));

}

**makeLaserBall(penalty) --- FULL REPLACEMENT**

Replace the existing makeLaserBall entirely.

function makeLaserBall(penalty) {

const container = new PIXI.Container();

const type = getFireballType(penalty);

if (!type) {

// Zero penalty --- green glowing ring only, no fireball sprite

const ring = new PIXI.Graphics();

ring.lineStyle(3, 0x4ade80, 0.9);

ring.drawCircle(0, 0, 28);

// Outer soft glow ring

ring.lineStyle(8, 0x4ade80, 0.15);

ring.drawCircle(0, 0, 36);

container.addChild(ring);

container.\_isRing = true;

return container;

}

const frames = fireballTextures\[type\];

const anim = new PIXI.AnimatedSprite(frames);

anim.anchor.set(0.5, 0.5);

// Rotate so side-facing fireball points downward (trail goes up)

anim.rotation = Math.PI / 2;

// Scale: base size proportional to penalty intensity

const t = Math.min(penalty / 100, 1);

const baseScale = 0.18 + t \* 0.22; // 0.18 at low penalty тЖТ 0.40 at max

anim.scale.set(baseScale);

// Animation speed: same for all (size conveys intensity, not speed)

anim.animationSpeed = 0.4;

anim.loop = true;

anim.play();

container.addChild(anim);

container.\_anim = anim;

container.\_isRing = false;

return container;

}

**scaleBallToWeight(ball, weight)**

After Phase A (penalty ball materialized), grow ball to weighted size:

function scaleBallToWeight(ball, weight, penalty) {

return new Promise(resolve =\> {

if (ball.\_isRing) { resolve(); return; }

const anim = ball.\_anim;

const t = Math.min(penalty / 100, 1);

const baseScale = 0.18 + t \* 0.22;

const weightedScale = baseScale + weight \* 0.35; // heavier weight = bigger fireball

const startScale = anim.scale.x;

let tick = 0;

const fn = () =\> {

tick += 0.025;

const ease = 1 - Math.pow(1 - Math.min(tick, 1), 3);

const s = startScale + (weightedScale - startScale) \* ease;

anim.scale.set(s);

if (tick \>= 1) { app.ticker.remove(fn); resolve(); }

};

app.ticker.add(fn);

});

}

**startPulse(ball) --- idle float animation**

function startPulse(ball) {

let t = 0;

const fn = () =\> {

t += 0.035;

ball.y += Math.sin(t) \* 0.4; // gentle vertical float

};

app.ticker.add(fn);

return fn; // caller stores and removes this reference

}

**fireBall(ball, pulseFn, targetY) --- drop animation**

function fireBall(ball, pulseFn, targetY) {

return new Promise(resolve =\> {

app.ticker.remove(pulseFn);

const startY = ball.y;

let t = 0;

const fn = () =\> {

t += 0.02;

const ease = Math.pow(Math.min(t, 1), 2); // ease-in, accelerates downward

ball.y = startY + (targetY - startY) \* ease;

if (t \>= 1) {

app.ticker.remove(fn);

fxL.removeChild(ball);

if (ball.\_anim) ball.\_anim.stop();

resolve();

}

};

app.ticker.add(fn);

});

}

**Impact Flash**

function flashImpact(x, y, penalty) {

const color = penalty \< 0.01 ? 0x4ade80 : penalty \< 50 ? 0xff9900 : 0xff2200;

const flash = new PIXI.Graphics();

flash.beginFill(color, 0.7);

flash.drawCircle(x, y, 40);

flash.endFill();

fxL.addChild(flash);

let t = 0;

const fn = () =\> {

t += 0.06;

flash.alpha = 1 - t;

flash.scale.set(1 + t \* 0.8);

if (t \>= 1) { app.ticker.remove(fn); fxL.removeChild(flash); }

};

app.ticker.add(fn);

}

**laserCriterion(fi) --- Full Sequence**

Replace existing stepCriterion / laserCriterion with this exact sequence:

1\. setNarrator(narration\[fi\], \'explaining\')

2\. showBadge(feat, weight) + showIdealBadge(DEMO.ideals\[feat\])

3\. drawValuesZone(feat) тЖР highlights active feature row

4\. await delay(1000)

тФАтФА PHASE A: Materialize balls one by one тФАтФА

5\. For i = 0 to N-1:

a\. penalty = DEMO.detailed_breakdown\[candidate\]\[feat\].penalty (raw penalty, NOT weighted)

b\. Show math text for this candidate (left-aligned block, see Math Text spec below)

Line 1: \`\${feat}: \${raw} тЖТ norm: \${normed}\`

Line 2: \`Penalty = max(0, \${normedIdeal.toFixed(1)} тИТ \${normed.toFixed(1)}) = \${penalty.toFixed(1)}\`

c\. ball = makeLaserBall(penalty)

d\. ball.x = CENTERS\[i\]

e\. ball.y = BALL_ZONE_Y

f\. fxL.addChild(ball)

g\. pulseFns\[i\] = startPulse(ball)

h\. balls\[i\] = ball

i\. await delay(1400) тЖР user reads the math, sees ball appear

6\. await delay(1000) тЖР all 3 balls visible, pause so user sees them together

тФАтФА PHASE B: Apply weight, fire one by one тФАтФА

7\. For i = 0 to N-1:

a\. weightedPenalty = DEMO.detailed_breakdown\[candidate\]\[feat\].weighted_penalty

b\. Update math text line 2 for this candidate:

\`Weighted = \${penalty.toFixed(1)} ├Ч \${weight.toFixed(2)} = \${weightedPenalty.toFixed(1)}\`

c\. await scaleBallToWeight(balls\[i\], weight, penalty) тЖР ball grows

d\. await delay(600)

e\. targetY = GROUND_Y + platSink\[i\] - CHAR_H \* 0.1

f\. await fireBall(balls\[i\], pulseFns\[i\], targetY)

g\. flashImpact(CENTERS\[i\], targetY, weightedPenalty)

h\. runPenalty\[i\] += weightedPenalty

i\. if (weightedPenalty \< 0.01): show green tick floatTxt at impact point

j\. else: await sinkPlatform(i, (weightedPenalty/100)\*MAX_SINK)

k\. await updateEmos() тЖР sequential emotion update

l\. await delay(500)

8\. clearMathTexts()

9\. Narrator reaction based on current leader

10\. await delay(600)

# Codex Prompt 96 : Fixing Errors

**Visual Fixes 1-4 --- Codex Spec**

**Fix 1 --- Math Text Above Each Individual Candidate (not left-aligned block)**

**Current behavior**

All 3 candidates\' math text is stacked in a left-aligned column at x=20.

**Required behavior**

Each candidate\'s math text floats centered above THEIR OWN column.

-   Alice math text тЖТ centered at x = CENTERS\[0\]

-   Bob math text тЖТ centered at x = CENTERS\[1\]

-   Charlie math text тЖТ centered at x = CENTERS\[2\]

**Implementation**

In showMathText(charIndex, line1, line2):

// x position = CENTERS\[charIndex\]

// anchor = (0.5, 0) for center-aligned text

// y position:

// line1: MATH_ZONE_Y + 10

// line2: MATH_ZONE_Y + 32

// Font: Courier New, 13px, white (0xffffff)

// dropShadow: true, dropShadowDistance: 2, dropShadowColor: 0x000000

// No colored prefix label like \"\[Alice\]\" --- remove that

Each candidate\'s text appears one at a time (as Phase A already does them sequentially). Text for candidate i replaces or stacks --- do NOT show all 3 simultaneously until all 3 are done. Actually: KEEP all previous candidates\' text visible as each new one appears. So after Alice\'s text appears, Bob\'s appears below or beside --- but centered above their own column.

**Fix 2 --- Name Inside Platform, Remove Name Label Above Character**

**Remove**

The floating name label above each character (currently nameLbls array drawn in spawnLabels()). Remove spawnLabels() call from init() and restartVisualization(). Remove updateLabelPositions() call from redraw().

**Add --- Name on Platform**

In drawPlatforms(), after drawing the platform body, add a PIXI.Text for the candidate name:

const nameTxt = new PIXI.Text(DEMO.candidates\[i\], {

fontSize: 15,

fill: 0xffffff,

fontWeight: \'bold\',

dropShadow: true,

dropShadowColor: 0x000000,

dropShadowDistance: 1,

});

nameTxt.anchor.set(0.5, 0.5);

nameTxt.x = cx;

nameTxt.y = py + PLAT_H / 2; // vertically centered on platform

platL.addChild(nameTxt);

Remove the separate penalty score text that currently overlaps below platform. Instead show penalty score BELOW platform as before but WITHOUT the name --- just the score number.

**Fix 3 --- Zero Penalty: Show Text Instead of Green Ring**

**Remove**

The green ring graphic (ball.\_isRing path in makeLaserBall). Do not create any PIXI.Graphics for zero penalty case.

**Replace with**

When penalty \< 0.01, instead of returning a ring container:

// Return a special container with a PIXI.Text

const txt = new PIXI.Text(\'ЁЯШЗ No Penalty --- No Fire тШ║я╕П\', {

fontFamily: \'-apple-system, BlinkMacSystemFont, sans-serif\',

fontSize: 16,

fontWeight: \'bold\',

fill: 0xffffff,

dropShadow: true,

dropShadowColor: 0x000000,

dropShadowDistance: 2,

});

txt.anchor.set(0.5, 0.5);

container.addChild(txt);

container.\_isRing = true; // keep flag so fireBall/scaleBallToWeight skip animation

container.\_isText = true;

return container;

In fireBall(): when ball.\_isText === true, just fade out and resolve immediately:

if (ball.\_isText) {

let t = 0;

const fn = () =\> {

t += 0.04;

ball.alpha = 1 - t;

if (t \>= 1) { app.ticker.remove(fn); fxL.removeChild(ball); resolve(); }

};

app.ticker.add(fn);

return;

}

In startPulse(): when ball.\_isText === true, do a gentle scale pulse:

if (ball.\_isText) {

let t = 0;

const fn = () =\> { t += 0.03; ball.scale.set(1 + Math.sin(t) \* 0.04); };

app.ticker.add(fn);

return fn;

}

In scaleBallToWeight(): when ball.\_isRing === true, resolve immediately (no change). Already handled.

**Fix 4 --- Larger Initial Fireball Size**

**Current**

const baseScale = 0.18 + t \* 0.22; // 0.18 minimum

**Replace with**

const baseScale = 0.32 + t \* 0.28; // 0.32 minimum тЖТ 0.60 at max penalty

And weighted scale growth:

const weightedScale = baseScale + weight \* 0.45; // was 0.35, now 0.45

This makes even low-penalty fireballs clearly visible and readable as a fireball shape.

# Codex Prompt 98 : New Changes

**Visual Fixes 1-4 --- Codex Spec**

**Current behavior**

All 3 candidates\' math text is stacked in a left-aligned column at x=20.

**Required behavior**

-   Alice math text тЖТ centered at x = CENTERS\[0\]

-   Bob math text тЖТ centered at x = CENTERS\[1\]

// x position = CENTERS\[charIndex\]

// anchor = (0.5, 0) for center-aligned text

function showPenaltyLabel(charIndex, weightedPenalty) {

return new Promise(resolve =\> {

const txt = new PIXI.Text(\`-\${weightedPenalty.toFixed(1)}\`, {

fontFamily: \'-apple-system, sans-serif\',

fontSize: 22,

fontWeight: \'bold\',

fill: CHAR_COLORS\[charIndex\],

dropShadow: true,

dropShadowColor: 0x000000,

dropShadowDistance: 2,

});

txt.anchor.set(0.5, 0);

txt.x = CENTERS\[charIndex\];

txt.y = GROUND_Y + platSink\[charIndex\] + PLAT_H + 30;

txt.alpha = 0;

fxL.addChild(txt);

mathBoxes.push(txt); // so clearMathTexts removes it

let t = 0;

const fn = () =\> {

t += 0.04;

txt.alpha = Math.min(t, 1);

if (t \>= 1) { app.ticker.remove(fn); resolve(); }

};

app.ticker.add(fn);

});

}

function getFireballType(penalty) {

if (penalty \< 0.01) return null;

if (penalty \<= 20) return \'fire_ball_side_small\';

if (penalty \<= 45) return \'fire_ball_side_medium\';

if (penalty \<= 70) return \'fireball_high_speed_side_small\';

if (penalty \<= 88) return \'meteor_side_medium\';

return \'fire_ball_blue_side_small\'; // highest penalty = blue, largest

}

function makeLaserBall(penalty) {

const type = getFireballType(penalty);

// Cap blue (highest tier) to prevent overlap

baseScale = Math.min(baseScale, 0.52);

}

// \...rest unchanged

}

**New State Variables**

Add at top of script alongside other state variables:

const penaltyLabelObjs = \[null, null, null\]; // LEFT penalty text per candidate

const valueBoxObjs = \[null, null, null\]; // RIGHT values box container per candidate

**New Function: showValuesBox(charIndex, activeFeature)**

Called at START of each laserCriterion (Phase A, for each candidate). Creates the right-side values box for candidate i.

function showValuesBox(charIndex, activeFeature) {

// Remove existing if any

if (valueBoxObjs\[charIndex\]) {

fxL.removeChild(valueBoxObjs\[charIndex\]);

valueBoxObjs\[charIndex\] = null;

}

const cx = CENTERS\[charIndex\];

const torsoY = GROUND_Y + platSink\[charIndex\] - CHAR_H \* 0.5;

const BOX_W = SLOT_W \* 0.28;

const BOX_H = 68;

const BOX_X = cx + SLOT_W \* 0.18; // right of character

const BOX_Y = torsoY - BOX_H / 2;

const container = new PIXI.Container();

container.\_charIndex = charIndex;

// Box background

const box = new PIXI.Graphics();

box.beginFill(0x0a0a28, 0.88);

box.drawRoundedRect(0, 0, BOX_W, BOX_H, 7);

box.endFill();

box.lineStyle(1.5, CHAR_COLORS\[charIndex\], 0.65);

box.drawRoundedRect(0, 0, BOX_W, BOX_H, 7);

container.addChild(box);

// Three value rows

const candidate = DEMO.candidates\[charIndex\];

const labels = \[\'S\', \'E\', \'C\'\];

const featKeys = DEMO.features; // \[\'Skills\', \'Experience\', \'Culture Fit\'\]

for (let fi = 0; fi \< 3; fi++) {

const feat = featKeys\[fi\];

const val = DEMO.raw\[candidate\]\[feat\];

const isActive = feat === activeFeature;

const rowTxt = new PIXI.Text(\`\${labels\[fi\]} : \${val}\`, {

fontFamily: \'Courier New\',

fontSize: 13,

fontWeight: isActive ? \'bold\' : \'normal\',

fill: isActive ? CHAR_COLORS\[charIndex\] : 0x9999bb,

dropShadow: false,

});

rowTxt.x = 10;

rowTxt.y = 8 + fi \* 20;

container.addChild(rowTxt);

}

container.x = BOX_X;

container.y = BOX_Y;

fxL.addChild(container);

valueBoxObjs\[charIndex\] = container;

}

**New Function: showPenaltyLabel(charIndex, weightedPenalty)**

Called AFTER fireball hits (Phase B, after sinkPlatform). Creates left-side penalty label for candidate i. Fades in over 400ms then stays static.

function showPenaltyLabel(charIndex, weightedPenalty) {

return new Promise(resolve =\> {

// Remove existing if any

if (penaltyLabelObjs\[charIndex\]) {

fxL.removeChild(penaltyLabelObjs\[charIndex\]);

penaltyLabelObjs\[charIndex\] = null;

}

const cx = CENTERS\[charIndex\];

const torsoY = GROUND_Y + platSink\[charIndex\] - CHAR_H \* 0.5;

const txt = new PIXI.Text(\`-\${weightedPenalty.toFixed(1)}\`, {

fontFamily: \'-apple-system, BlinkMacSystemFont, sans-serif\',

fontSize: 24,

fontWeight: \'bold\',

fill: CHAR_COLORS\[charIndex\],

dropShadow: true,

dropShadowColor: 0x000000,

dropShadowDistance: 2,

});

txt.anchor.set(1.0, 0.5); // right-aligned anchor

txt.x = cx - SLOT_W \* 0.18; // left of character

txt.y = torsoY;

txt.alpha = 0;

txt.\_charIndex = charIndex;

fxL.addChild(txt);

penaltyLabelObjs\[charIndex\] = txt;

// Fade in

let t = 0;

const fn = () =\> {

t += 0.04;

txt.alpha = Math.min(t, 1);

if (t \>= 1) { app.ticker.remove(fn); resolve(); }

};

app.ticker.add(fn);

});

}

**updateFloatingElements() --- Called Every Sink Tick**

function updateFloatingElements() {

for (let i = 0; i \< N; i++) {

const torsoY = GROUND_Y + platSink\[i\] - CHAR_H \* 0.5;

// Move penalty label (left side)

if (penaltyLabelObjs\[i\]) {

penaltyLabelObjs\[i\].y = torsoY;

}

// Move values box (right side)

if (valueBoxObjs\[i\]) {

const BOX_H = 68;

valueBoxObjs\[i\].y = torsoY - BOX_H / 2;

}

}

}

**Camera state:**

let cameraY = 0; // current gameWorld.y offset (negative = moved up)

let cameraTargetY = 0;

**updateCamera() --- called every frame in app.ticker**

app.ticker.add(() =\> {

// Smooth camera follow

if (Math.abs(gameWorld.y - cameraTargetY) \> 0.5) {

gameWorld.y += (cameraTargetY - gameWorld.y) \* 0.08;

} else {

gameWorld.y = cameraTargetY;

}

});

**recalcCameraTarget() --- called after each platSink update**

function recalcCameraTarget() {

// Find the lowest point across all candidates

// Lowest point = running total text position = GROUND_Y + platSink\[i\] + PLAT_H + 40

let lowestY = 0;

for (let i = 0; i \< N; i++) {

const bottom = GROUND_Y + platSink\[i\] + PLAT_H + 50;

if (bottom \> lowestY) lowestY = bottom;

}

// If lowest point exceeds visible canvas minus padding:

const margin = 50;

if (lowestY \> H - margin) {

cameraTargetY = -(lowestY - (H - margin));

}

// Never go above 0 (don\'t scroll up beyond start)

cameraTargetY = Math.min(cameraTargetY, 0);

}

**Call recalcCameraTarget() in sinkPlatform ticker:**

Inside sinkPlatform() ticker, after updating platSink\[charIndex\]:

recalcCameraTarget(); // тЖР ADD THIS every tick

**Reset camera on restart:**

In restartVisualization():

cameraY = 0;

cameraTargetY = 0;

gameWorld.y = 0;

**Important: fxL is inside gameWorld**

Since fxL is now inside gameWorld, all fireball positions, math boxes, penalty labels, values boxes --- their Y coordinates are already in gameWorld local space. No coordinate changes needed.

Replace stepNorm() content entirely:

async function stepNorm() {

clearMathTexts();

setNarrator(\"Normalization compresses all raw scores to a 0--100 scale so every criterion is judged fairly.\", \'explaining\');

hideBadge();

// Show one normalization box per candidate

for (let i = 0; i \< N; i++) {

const candidate = DEMO.candidates\[i\];

const BOX_W = SLOT_W \* 0.52;

const BOX_H = 82;

const cx = CENTERS\[i\];

const cy = GROUND_Y - CHAR_H \* 0.6; // above character

const container = new PIXI.Container();

// Box background

const box = new PIXI.Graphics();

box.beginFill(0x0a0a28, 0.9);

box.drawRoundedRect(0, 0, BOX_W, BOX_H, 8);

box.endFill();

box.lineStyle(1.5, CHAR_COLORS\[i\], 0.6);

box.drawRoundedRect(0, 0, BOX_W, BOX_H, 8);

container.addChild(box);

// Three normalization rows

for (let fi = 0; fi \< DEMO.features.length; fi++) {

const feat = DEMO.features\[fi\];

const raw = DEMO.raw\[candidate\]\[feat\];

const norm = DEMO.normed\[candidate\]\[feat\];

const rowTxt = new PIXI.Text(\`\${feat}: \${raw} тЖТ norm: \${norm.toFixed(1)}\`, {

fontFamily: \'Courier New\',

fontSize: 12,

fill: 0xaaaaff,

dropShadow: false,

});

rowTxt.x = 10;

rowTxt.y = 8 + fi \* 24;

container.addChild(rowTxt);

}

container.x = cx - BOX_W / 2;

container.y = cy - BOX_H / 2;

fxL.addChild(container);

mathBoxes.push(container);

}

// Stay visible --- do NOT clearMathTexts here

// Cleared at start of next laserCriterion (Fix 6 from previous spec)

document.getElementById(\'next-btn\').textContent = \`Apply: \${DEMO.features\[0\]} тЖТ\`;

}

**Add JS Functions**

function manualScroll(deltaPx) {

// deltaPx negative = scroll up (camera moves up = scene moves down visually)

// deltaPx positive = scroll down

cameraTargetY -= deltaPx;

// Clamp: never scroll above origin, never scroll below max sink

const maxDown = -(MAX_SINK \* 1.2);

cameraTargetY = Math.max(cameraTargetY, maxDown);

cameraTargetY = Math.min(cameraTargetY, 0);

}

function scrollToTop() {

cameraTargetY = 0;

// Smooth ticker already handles animation back to 0

}

**Auto Pan To Top After All Camera Movements Done**

After the last criterion\'s Phase B completes (all 3 candidates processed), add at the END of laserCriterion(fi) when fi === DEMO.features.length - 1:

// After last criterion narrator reaction + delay:

if (fi === DEMO.features.length - 1) {

scrollToTop(); // gently pan back to top so winner reveal looks clean

await delay(900); // wait for camera to finish panning

}

-   Fireball sprites: weisinx7 itch.io pack, 5 types, 30-40 frames each

-   Iterative design decisions: orb тЖТ fireball, left-right layout, auto-follow camera

# Codex Prompt 119 : Integrating prototype with real data

Here\'s what the spec covers and why each decision was made:

3 files, clear separation of concerns:

decisionLogic.js --- The only tricky part is that d\[i\]\[y\] gets overwritten by the penalty value inside the scoring loop. So the spec captures normedValues as a snapshot before that loop runs, not after. Miss that timing and you\'d store penalty scores instead of normalized values --- a silent bug that would be hard to trace.

server.js --- One line addition: raw: products_data. The normed and normedIdeals fields come through automatically via \...result spread since they\'re now returned by calculateDecision().

script.js --- Uses sessionStorage rather than URL params or localStorage because the data can be large (many products ├Ч many features) and sessionStorage is tab-scoped so it auto-cleans on tab close. The visualizer consumes and immediately deletes the key (removeItem) so a manual reload of the visualizer falls back to the demo cleanly.

visualizer_prototype.html --- The loadDemoData() pattern means the fallback demo is preserved exactly, the file stays standalone-runnable, and real data is opt-in. The dynamic N changes are minimal --- most loops already used N, the main fixes are the array initializations and the hardcoded \<3\> inside showValuesBox. **\# CHANGES_real.md**

**\## Integrate Visualizer with Real \`/api/calculate\` Response Data**

*\*Spec for Codex. Apply changes precisely. DO NOT change anything not listed here.\**

\-\--

**\## Overview**

The visualizer at \`frontend/visualizer_prototype.html\` currently uses a hardcoded \`DEMO\`

object. The goal is to make it consume **\*\*real data\*\*** passed from \`script.js\` after a

successful \`/api/calculate\` response.

Three files are modified:

\| File \| Change \|

\|\-\-\-\-\--\|\-\-\-\-\-\-\--\|

\| \`backend/decisionLogic.js\` \| Return \`raw\`, \`normed\`, \`normedIdeals\` in \`calculateDecision()\` \|

\| \`backend/server.js\` \| Forward those fields in the \`/api/calculate\` response \|

\| \`frontend/script.js\` \| After results, add \"Animate Result ЁЯОм\" button; pass data to visualizer via \`sessionStorage\` \|

\| \`frontend/visualizer_prototype.html\` \| On load, read \`sessionStorage\`; if present replace \`DEMO\`; otherwise keep hardcoded DEMO \|

\-\--

**\## CHANGE 1 --- \`backend/decisionLogic.js\`**

**\### Where: inside \`calculateDecision()\` function**

The function currently builds \`d\` (normalized values), \`norm_req_list\` (normalized ideals),

\`agg_sum\`, and \`detailed_breakdown\`, then returns them.

We need to **\*\*capture intermediate normalized values\*\*** before they get overwritten by penalty

scores, and return them.

**\### Step 1A --- Capture \`normedValues\` before penalty overwrites \`d\`**

Find this block (it comes just after the second normalization loop, before \`agg_sum = {}\`):

\`\`\`js

┬а const agg_sum = {};

┬а const detailed_breakdown = {};

┬а for (const i in d) {

┬а ┬а let tsum = 0;

┬а ┬а detailed_breakdown\[i\] = {};

┬а ┬а for (let x = 0; x \< f_list.length; x++) {

┬а ┬а ┬а const y = f_list\[x\];

┬а ┬а ┬а let penalty;

┬а ┬а ┬а \...

┬а ┬а ┬а d\[i\]\[y\] = penalty; ┬а // тЖР THIS LINE overwrites the normalized value with penalty

\`\`\`

**\*\*Before\*\*** the \`agg_sum = {}\` line, add:

\`\`\`js

┬а // Snapshot normalized values before penalty calculation overwrites d

┬а const normedValues = {};

┬а for (const p in d) {

┬а ┬а normedValues\[p\] = {};

┬а ┬а for (const f of f_list) {

┬а ┬а ┬а normedValues\[p\]\[f\] = parseFloat(d\[p\]\[f\].toFixed(4));

┬а ┬а }

┬а }

\`\`\`

**\### Step 1B --- Build \`normedIdeals\` map**

Immediately after the \`norm_req_list\` array is fully built (after the for loop that pushes

to it), add:

\`\`\`js

┬а // Build named map of normalized ideal values

┬а const normedIdeals = {};

┬а for (let i = 0; i \< f_list.length; i++) {

┬а ┬а normedIdeals\[f_list\[i\]\] = parseFloat(norm_req_list\[i\].toFixed(4));

┬а }

\`\`\`

**\### Step 1C --- Return the new fields**

Find the \`return {\` statement at the end of \`calculateDecision()\`. It currently returns:

\`\`\`js

┬а return {

┬а ┬а winner: tie.length === 1 ? tie\[0\] : null,

┬а ┬а tie,

┬а ┬а ranking,

┬а ┬а agg_sum,

┬а ┬а detailed_breakdown,

┬а ┬а weights,

┬а ┬а features: f_list,

┬а ┬а directions: high_or_low,

┬а };

\`\`\`

Change it to:

\`\`\`js

┬а return {

┬а ┬а winner: tie.length === 1 ? tie\[0\] : null,

┬а ┬а tie,

┬а ┬а ranking,

┬а ┬а agg_sum,

┬а ┬а detailed_breakdown,

┬а ┬а weights,

┬а ┬а features: f_list,

┬а ┬а directions: high_or_low,

┬а ┬а normed: normedValues, ┬а ┬а ┬а // { ProductName: { FeatureName: 0-100 } }

┬а ┬а normedIdeals, ┬а ┬а ┬а ┬а ┬а ┬а ┬а // { FeatureName: 0-100 }

┬а };

\`\`\`

**\### DO NOT CHANGE in decisionLogic.js:**

\- \`preprocessInputs()\`

\- \`extractScoreFromText()\`

\- \`generateExplanation()\`

\- \`build4Styles()\`

\- \`SCALE_MAP\`

\- Any explanation builder functions

\-\--

**\## CHANGE 2 --- \`backend/server.js\`**

**\### Where: inside \`POST /api/calculate\` handler**

The handler currently calls \`calculateDecision()\` and spreads the result:

\`\`\`js

┬а ┬а res.json({

┬а ┬а ┬а \...result,

┬а ┬а ┬а explanation,

┬а ┬а ┬а explanation_source: source,

┬а ┬а ┬а explanation_styles: styles,

┬а ┬а });

\`\`\`

The spread \`\...result\` will automatically include the new \`normed\` and \`normedIdeals\`

fields once Change 1 is applied. **\*\*No additional code needed here.\*\***

However, we also need to pass \`raw\` (the original user-entered values) so the visualizer

can display them. \`products_data\` is already available in the handler scope as it comes

from \`req.body\`.

Change the \`res.json(\...)\` call to:

\`\`\`js

┬а ┬а res.json({

┬а ┬а ┬а \...result,

┬а ┬а ┬а explanation,

┬а ┬а ┬а explanation_source: source,

┬а ┬а ┬а explanation_styles: styles,

┬а ┬а ┬а raw: products_data, ┬а // original user-entered values, shape: { ProductName: { FeatureName: value } }

┬а ┬а });

\`\`\`

**\### DO NOT CHANGE in server.js:**

\- \`/api/preprocess\` route

\- \`app.use(express.static(\...))\` line

\- \`app.listen(\...)\` line

\- Any import/require statements

\-\--

**\## CHANGE 3 --- \`frontend/script.js\`**

**\### Where: inside \`displayResults(result)\` function**

function sets \`container.innerHTML = html\`. We need to:

1\. Store the full result in \`sessionStorage\` (serialized as JSON) under key

┬а ┬а\`\"visualizerData\"\`.

\`\`\`js

┬а ┬а container.innerHTML = html;

\`\`\`

**\*\*Replace it with:\*\***

\`\`\`js

┬а ┬а // Store result for visualizer

┬а ┬а try {

┬а ┬а ┬а sessionStorage.setItem(\'visualizerData\', JSON.stringify({

┬а ┬а ┬а ┬а candidates: result.ranking.map(r =\> r.product),

┬а ┬а ┬а ┬а features: result.features,

┬а ┬а ┬а ┬а weights: result.weights,

┬а ┬а ┬а ┬а raw: result.raw,

┬а ┬а ┬а ┬а ranking: result.ranking,

┬а ┬а ┬а ┬а winner: result.winner,

┬а ┬а ┬а ┬а explanation: result.explanation,

┬а ┬а ┬а }));

┬а ┬а } catch(e) {

┬а ┬а ┬а console.warn(\'sessionStorage not available:\', e);

┬а ┬а }

┬а ┬а html += \`

┬а ┬а ┬а \<div style=\"margin-top: 24px; text-align: center;\"\>

┬а ┬а ┬а ┬а \<button onclick=\"openVisualizer()\" class=\"btn-primary\" style=\"font-size:1.1rem; padding: 14px 32px;\"\>

┬а ┬а ┬а ┬а ┬а ЁЯОм Animate Result

┬а ┬а ┬а ┬а \</button\>

┬а ┬а ┬а \</div\>

┬а ┬а \`;

┬а ┬а container.innerHTML = html;

\`\`\`

**\## CHANGE 4 --- \`frontend/visualizer_prototype.html\`**

**\### Where: the \`// тФАтФА DEMO DATA тФАтФА\` block and \`init()\` function**

This is the most significant change. The visualizer currently has a hardcoded \`DEMO\`

object at the top of the \`\<script\>\` tag. We need it to:

1\. On load, check \`sessionStorage\` for \`\"visualizerData\"\`

2\. If found тЖТ parse it and use as \`DEMO\`, then clear the key

3\. If NOT found тЖТ keep the existing hardcoded \`DEMO\` as fallback (so the demo still

┬а ┬аworks standalone)

function loadDemoData() {

┬а try {

┬а ┬а const stored = sessionStorage.getItem(\'visualizerData\');

┬а ┬а if (stored) {

┬а ┬а ┬а sessionStorage.removeItem(\'visualizerData\'); // consume once

┬а ┬а ┬а const d = JSON.parse(stored);

┬а ┬а ┬а // Validate minimum required fields

┬а ┬а ┬а if (

┬а ┬а ┬а ┬а Array.isArray(d.candidates) && d.candidates.length \>= 2 &&

┬а ┬а ┬а ┬а Array.isArray(d.features) ┬а && d.features.length \>= 1 &&

┬а ┬а ┬а ┬а Array.isArray(d.weights) ┬а ┬а&&

┬а ┬а ┬а ┬а d.raw && d.normed && d.normedIdeals &&

┬а ┬а ┬а ┬а d.detailed_breakdown && d.ranking && d.winner

┬а ┬а ┬а ) {

┬а ┬а ┬а ┬а console.log(\'\[Visualizer\] Using real data for:\', d.candidates);

┬а ┬а ┬а ┬а return d;

┬а ┬а ┬а }

┬а ┬а }

┬а } catch(e) {

┬а ┬а console.warn(\'\[Visualizer\] sessionStorage read failed:\', e);

┬а }

┬а console.log(\'\[Visualizer\] Using fallback DEMO data\');

┬а return DEMO_FALLBACK;

}

const DEMO = loadDemoData();

Antigravity Sonnet tried to fix it : Root Cause Analysis There were two bugs preventing real data from reaching the visualizer: Bug 1 --- Wrong storage API (

sessionStorage

тЖТ

localStorage

)

sessionStorage

is tab-scoped --- each new browser tab gets its own isolated session storage. When

window.open(\'/visualizer_prototype.html\', \'\_blank\')

opens a new tab, that tab has an empty sessionStorage and never sees the data stored by the parent tab.

Fix: Changed both script.js and visualizer_prototype.html to use

localStorage

, which is shared across all tabs of the same origin.

Bug 2 --- Null winner breaks validation The loadDemoData() validator checked

d.winner

as a truthy value. But

result.winner

is

null

when all candidates tie (epsilon \< 0.001). A tied result would silently fall back to the demo.

Fix: Changed

d.winner

тЖТ

\'winner\' in d

--- a structural check that passes for

null

values.

Verification

Validation PASSES: true

Tie case (winner=null) validation PASSES: true All 10 required fields (

candidates

,

features

,

weights

, raw,

normed

,

normedIdeals

,

detailed_breakdown

,

ranking

,

winner

,

explanation

) are confirmed present in the API response chain.

To test: Run

cd backend && npm run dev

, complete a decision, and click ЁЯОм Animate Result --- the visualizer console should now say

\[Visualizer\] Using real data for: \[your candidates\]

instead of the fallback message.

# Prompt 122 : Server.js checked

Yes, You may also Verify app.post(\"/api/calculate\", async (req, res) =\> {

try {

const { products_data, features, weights_raw, ideals, directions, metadata } =

req.body;

const result = calculateDecision(products_data, features, weights_raw, ideals, directions);

// Attach input source metadata so the frontend can show badges

if (metadata) {

for (const product of Object.keys(result.detailed_breakdown)) {

for (const feature of features) {

if (metadata\[product\]?.\[feature\]) {

result.detailed_breakdown\[product\]\[feature\].inputSource =

metadata\[product\]\[feature\].source;

result.detailed_breakdown\[product\]\[feature\].confidence =

metadata\[product\]\[feature\].confidence;

}

}

}

}

// Generate AI narrative explanation (Phase 1 --- unchanged)

const { explanation, source } = await generateExplanation(result, features, products_data);

const styles = build4Styles(result, features, products_data);

res.json({

\...result,

explanation,

explanation_source: source,

explanation_styles: styles,

raw: products_data,

});

} catch (error) {

console.error(\"Calculation error:\", error.message);

res.status(500).json({ error: error.message });

}

});

# Prompt 128 : Starting Phase 2

-   What was the issue I diagnosed The app was running a stale runtime context (cached/old frontend asset or wrong file copy), so the visualizer booted before valid injected payload was visible and kept falling back to demo. Your logs (fallback + loadInjectedData() called) indicated old parent behavior was still in play, not the intended current source path.

-   What solution I implemented I enforced a single runtime source-of-truth in served frontend files and added cache-busting/version markers so stale copies cannot win:

    1.  index.html: versioned script include (script.js?v=runtime-source-fix-2026-02-25-1).

    2.  script.js: parent window now stores **VISUALIZER_DATA** + **VISUALIZER_SOURCE** before iframe boot, and iframe loads with cache-busted URL (/visualizer_prototype.html?build=\...&ts=\...).

    3.  visualizer_prototype.html: logs build + parent source, reads injected parent data first, and logs explicit validation failure reason when injected payload is present but invalid.

-   

That worked What was the issue diagnosed

1.  Garbled UI text came from mojibake literals in visualizer_prototype.html (narrator title, watch-again text, and penalty prefix strings).

2.  Scroll controls only moved vertical camera target; there was no horizontal camera/world behavior, so they felt ineffective for larger candidate counts.

3.  Character assignment was fixed-length, so scaling beyond existing slots wasn't truly generic, and char4/char5 were not wired into sprite loading. What was the solution implemented

4.  Fixed visible text literals to clean ASCII in visualizer_prototype.html:

    -   THE ANALYST at visualizer_prototype.html (line 355)

    -   Watch Again at visualizer_prototype.html (line 378)

    -   cumulative label now Penalty: \... at visualizer_prototype.html (line 673)

5.  Added real canvas scrolling support:

    -   World/camera horizontal logic (cameraTargetX, clamp, slider sync, manual X scroll) at visualizer_prototype.html (line 593), visualizer_prototype.html (line 764), visualizer_prototype.html (line 808), visualizer_prototype.html (line 813)
